import torch
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoConfig

class Model(torch.nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, model_name, config):
        super().__init__()
        self.model_name = model_name
        self.config = config
        self.model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(self.model_name, config=self.config)

    def forward(self, x):
        return self.model(x).logits

model_name = "google/bigbird-roberta-base"
config = AutoConfig.from_pretrained(model_name)
vocab_size = config.vocab_size
sequence_length = 4095
batch_size = 1

def get_inputs():
    inputs = torch.randint(0, vocab_size, (batch_size, sequence_length))
    return [inputs]

def get_init_inputs():
    return [model_name, config]

For a full forward pass, the model weights are approximately: - 12 layers × (4 projections + FFN1 + FFN2 + 2 LayerNorms) - Embeddings: 50265 × 768 ≈ 38.6M - Per layer: 4×(768×768) + 768×3072 + 3072×768 + 2×768 ≈ 2.36M + 2.36M + 1.5K ≈ 4.7M - 12 layers: ~56.4M - LM head: 50265 × 768 ≈ 38.6M Total weights: ~134M parameters ≈ 536 MB (fp32) or 268 MB (bf16) Activation memory per layer: batch_size × seq_len × hidden_size × layers = 1 × 4095 × 768 × 12 ≈ 37.8M floats ≈ 151 MB (fp32) The model is weight-bound for single batch. Reading 268MB of weights at 3.35TB/s takes ~80 microseconds... but that's at peak bandwidth which GEMMs don't achieve. Realistically, each GEMM needs to read its inputs and weights and write outputs. For M=4095, N=3072, K=768: - Weight bytes: 3072×768×2 = 4.7MB (bf16) - Input bytes: 4095×768×2 = 6.3MB - Output bytes: 4095×3072×2 = 25.2MB - Total memory traffic: ~36MB at minimum 12 layers × 4 GEMMs = 48 GEMMs × 36MB = 1.7GB of memory traffic At 3.35TB/s = ~0.5ms This seems way too optimistic. Real kernel implementations have much lower effective bandwidth due to tiling, shared memory traffic, etc. But this tells me the PyTorch reference should be quite fast already. To get a significant speedup, I'd need to: 1. Use more efficient kernels (cuBLASLt might help) 2. Fuse operations to reduce memory traffic 3. Let me write a better layer norm kernel: ```cuda #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cub/cub.cuh> // Can I use cub? Usually yes in PyTorch extensions __global__ void layer_norm_kernel(...) { // One block per row // hidden_size threads per block // Use shared memory for reduction } ``` Actually, to keep it simple and correct, let me use a straightforward implementation. For hidden_size=768, I can have 256 threads per block doing 3 elements each, or 768 threads. Wait, on H100, max threads per block is 1024, so 768 is fine. But to maximize occupancy, fewer threads (like 256) might be better, with each thread handling 3 elements. For mean and variance computation, I need a parallel reduction. I can either use shared memory with syncthreads, or use warp shuffle instructions. Let me write a simpler but correct kernel using CUB for reduction. CUB is usually available in PyTorch CUDA extensions. Actually, for simplicity and to avoid CUB dependency issues, let me use a manual reduction: ```cuda template <int HIDDEN_SIZE> __global__ void layer_norm_kernel( const float* input, const float* gamma, const float* beta, float* output, int num_rows, float eps) { int row = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; if (row >= num_rows) return; const float* row_input = input + row * HIDDEN_SIZE; float* row_output = output + row * HIDDEN_SIZE; // Reduction for mean float sum = 0.0f; for (int i = tid; i < HIDDEN_SIZE; i += blockDim.x) { sum += row_input[i]; } // Warp reduce for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, sum, offset); } __shared__ float shared_mean; if (tid == 0) shared_mean = sum / HIDDEN_SIZE; __syncthreads(); float mean = shared_mean; // Reduction for variance sum = 0.0f; for (int i = tid; i < HIDDEN_SIZE; i += blockDim.x) { float diff = row_input[i] - mean; sum += diff * diff; } for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, sum, offset); } __shared__ float shared_var; if (tid == 0) shared_var = sum / HIDDEN_SIZE; __syncthreads(); float inv_std = rsqrtf(shared_var + eps); // Write output for (int i = tid; i < HIDDEN_SIZE; i += blockDim.x) { float val = (row_input[i] - mean) * inv_std; row_output[i] = val * gamma[i] + beta[i]; } } ``` This is a simple and correct layer norm kernel. For hidden_size=768, with 256 threads, each thread handles 3 elements in a strided fashion. The warp reduction works because 256 is a multiple of 32. Wait, there's a subtlety. For BigBird's specific parameters, let me write a generic transformer forward in C++: ```cpp torch::Tensor custom_forward( torch::Tensor input_ids, torch::Tensor word_embeddings, torch::Tensor position_embeddings, // ... lots of weight tensors ... ) { // Embedding lookup auto hidden = at::embedding(word_embeddings, input_ids); hidden = hidden + position_embeddings.unsqueeze(0); for (int i = 0; i < num_layers; i++) { // Layer norm auto normed = at::layer_norm(hidden, {hidden_size}, gamma1[i], beta1[i], eps, true); // Attention projections auto q = at::linear(normed, w_q[i], b_q[i]); auto k = at::linear(normed, w_k[i], b_k[i]); auto v = at::linear(normed, w_v[i], b_v[i]); // Reshape for multi-head attention q = q.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).transpose(1, 2); k = k.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).transpose(1, 2); v = v.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).transpose(1, 2); // Scaled dot-product attention auto attn_out = at::scaled_dot_product_attention(q, k, v); // Reshape back and project attn_out = attn_out.transpose(1, 2).reshape({batch_size, seq_len, hidden_size}); attn_out = at::linear(attn_out, w_o[i], b_o[i]); // Residual hidden = hidden + attn_out; // FFN auto normed2 = at::layer_norm(hidden, {hidden_size}, gamma2[i], beta2[i], eps, true); auto ffn1 = at::linear(normed2, w_ffn1[i], b_ffn1[i]); ffn1 = at::gelu(ffn1); auto ffn2 = at::linear(ffn1, w_ffn2[i], b_ffn2[i]); hidden = hidden + ffn2; } // Final layer norm and LM head hidden = at::layer_norm(hidden, {hidden_size}, gamma_final, beta_final, eps, true); auto logits = at::linear(hidden, w_lm_head, b_lm_head); return logits; } ``` This is clean and straightforward. But there are issues: 1. `at::layer_norm` might not be the exact same as `nn.LayerNorm` depending on implementation details 2. For BigBird, attention might be different 3. Let me write the CUDA code for LayerNorm: ```cuda #include <torch/extension.h> template <typename T> __device__ __forceinline__ T warpReduceSum(T val) { #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) val += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, val, offset); return val; } __global__ void layer_norm_kernel( const float* input, const float* gamma, const float* beta, float* output, int hidden_size, float eps, int num_rows) { int row = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; if (row >= num_rows) return; const float* row_in = input + row * hidden_size; float* row_out = output + row * hidden_size; float sum = 0.0f; for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { sum += row_in[i]; } sum = warpReduceSum(sum); __shared__ float mean; if (tid % 32 == 0) { atomicAdd(&mean, sum); } __syncthreads(); if (tid == 0) { mean = mean / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); // Same for variance float var_sum = 0.0f; for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float diff = row_in[i] - mean; var_sum += diff * diff; } var_sum = warpReduceSum(var_sum); __shared__ float variance; if (tid % 32 == 0) { atomicAdd(&variance, var_sum); } __syncthreads(); if (tid == 0) { variance = variance / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); float inv_std = rsqrtf(variance + eps); for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float val = (row_in[i] - mean) * inv_std; row_out[i] = val * gamma[i] + beta[i]; } } ``` Wait, there's a bug with `atomicAdd` on shared memory. `atomicAdd` works but for shared memory floats it's special. Actually `atomicAdd(&mean, sum)` on shared memory in the same block should work OK because all warps are in the same block. But only the first thread in each warp writes, and there are `blockDim.x / 32` warps. However, `atomicAdd` for float might not be available on all architectures? No, it's available since compute capability 2.x for global memory and 6.x for shared memory. H100 is 9.0, so it should work. But a cleaner approach is to use shared memory with a proper reduction tree: ```cuda __shared__ float sdata[256]; // or dynamically sized sdata[tid] = sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 0; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } float mean = sdata[0] / hidden_size; ``` This is cleaner and doesn't need atomics. Let me use this approach. For blockDim.x, I need it to be a power of 2. If hidden_size=768, I can use 256 threads with 3 elements each, or 512 threads with 2 elements, or 128 threads with 6 elements. Using 256 threads: ```cuda float sum = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += 256) { sum += row_in[i]; } sdata[tid] = sum; __syncthreads(); // Reduction if (tid < 128) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 128]; __syncthreads(); if (tid < 64) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + 64]; __syncthreads(); // warp level if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, 32); // this doesn't make sense for < 32 threads } ``` Wait, for blockDim.x = 256: - After tid < 128: 128 values - After tid < 64: 64 values - For 64 values in 2 warps of 32: - We can do warp-level reduction for each warp - Then reduce the 2 warp results Let me write it cleanly: ```cuda __shared__ float sdata[256]; sdata[tid] = sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = 128; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, 16); v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, 8); v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, 4); v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, 2); v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, 1); if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v; } __syncthreads(); float mean = sdata[0] / hidden_size; ``` This is clean and correct for blockDim.x = 256. But if I want to support arbitrary blockDim.x, I need a generic version. Let me just fix blockDim.x at 256. BigBird should follow the same pattern. For the FFN, BERT uses: ``` ffn = linear1(hidden) # [B, S, 4H] (intermediate_size = 4 * hidden_size for BERT-base) ffn = gelu(ffn) ffn = linear2(ffn) # [B, S, H] ``` For BigBird-RoBERTa-base, the intermediate size should be 3072 (4 * 768). For the attention: ``` # Q, K, V projections q = linear_q(hidden) # [B, S, H] k = linear_k(hidden) # [B, S, H] v = linear_v(hidden) # [B, S, H] # Reshape for multi-head q = q.view(B, S, num_heads, head_dim).transpose(1, 2) # [B, H, S, D] k = k.view(B, S, num_heads, head_dim).transpose(1, 2) v = v.view(B, S, num_heads, head_dim).transpose(1, 2) # Scaled dot-product attention scores = matmul(q, k.transpose(-2, -1)) / sqrt(head_dim) # Apply attention mask scores = scores + attention_mask # causal mask or other mask probs = softmax(scores, dim=-1) probs = dropout(probs) attn = matmul(probs, v) # Reshape and project attn = attn.transpose(1, 2).reshape(B, S, H) attn = linear_o(attn) attn = dropout(attn) ``` And residual + layer norm after attention output. For a CausalLM from an encoder model, the causal mask is typically a lower-triangular mask or attention bias that prevents attending to future positions. In `at::scaled_dot_product_attention`, I can pass `is_causal=True` to get causal attention. But for BERT/RoBERTa, the original model doesn't use causal attention. When converted to CausalLM, it might. OK, let me write the implementation assuming causal attention. If it's wrong, I'll fix it. Actually, `at::scaled_dot_product_attention` in C++ doesn't have a simple `is_causal` parameter like the Python version. Let me check the C++ ATen API... I think it's: ```cpp at::Tensor at::_scaled_dot_product_attention( const at::Tensor& query, const at::Tensor& key, const at::Tensor& value, const c10::optional<at::Tensor>& attn_mask, double dropout_p, bool is_causal, c10::optional<double> scale ); ``` Actually, the exact signature might vary by PyTorch version. For PyTorch 2.0+, there's `at::_scaled_dot_product_attention`. I'll need to figure out the exact API or just use manual attention computation. For manual attention: ```cpp auto scores = at::matmul(q, k.transpose(-2, -1)); scores = scores / sqrt(head_dim); if (causal) { // Create causal mask auto causal_mask = at::triu(at::full({seq_len, seq_len}, -INFINITY, scores.options()), 1); scores = scores + causal_mask.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(0); } auto probs = at::softmax(scores, -1); probs = at::dropout(probs, dropout_p, /*training=*/false); auto attn = at::matmul(probs, v); ``` This is more verbose but works regardless of the PyTorch version. Here's my first draft of the C++ code: ```cpp #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cmath> // Simple custom CUDA kernel for LayerNorm __global__ void layer_norm_fused_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ output, int hidden_size, float eps, int num_rows) { int row = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; if (row >= num_rows) return; const float* row_in = input + row * hidden_size; float* row_out = output + row * hidden_size; extern __shared__ float sdata[]; float sum = 0.0f; for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { sum += row_in[i]; } sdata[tid] = sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); float mean = sdata[0]; float var_sum = 0.0f; for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float diff = row_in[i] - mean; var_sum += diff * diff; } sdata[tid] = var_sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); float variance = sdata[0]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(variance + eps); for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float val = (row_in[i] - mean) * inv_std; row_out[i] = val * gamma[i] + beta[i]; } } torch::Tensor custom_layer_norm(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor gamma, torch::Tensor beta, float eps) { int num_rows = input.size(0) * input.size(1); int hidden_size = input.size(2); auto output = torch::empty_like(input); int threads = 256; int shared_mem = threads * sizeof(float); layer_norm_fused_kernel<<<num_rows, threads, shared_mem>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), gamma.data_ptr<float>(), beta.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), hidden_size, eps, num_rows ); return output; } torch::Tensor transformer_forward( torch::Tensor input_ids, std::vector<torch::Tensor> params, int num_layers, int num_heads, float eps) { int param_idx = 0; auto word_emb = params[param_idx++]; auto pos_emb = params[param_idx++]; // might be a dummy tensor auto embed_ln_gamma = params[param_idx++]; auto embed_ln_beta = params[param_idx++]; // Embedding lookup auto hidden = torch::nn::functional::embedding(input_ids, word_emb); // Add position embeddings if not None if (pos_emb.dim() > 0 && pos_emb.numel() > 0) { hidden = hidden + pos_emb.unsqueeze(0); } // Embed layer norm hidden = custom_layer_norm(hidden, embed_ln_gamma, embed_ln_beta, eps); int batch_size = hidden.size(0); int seq_len = hidden.size(1); int hidden_size = hidden.size(2); int head_dim = hidden_size / num_heads; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf(head_dim); for (int layer = 0; layer < num_layers; layer++) { auto q_w = params[param_idx++]; auto q_b = params[param_idx++]; auto k_w = params[param_idx++]; auto k_b = params[param_idx++]; auto v_w = params[param_idx++]; auto v_b = params[param_idx++]; auto o_w = params[param_idx++]; auto o_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ln1_g = params[param_idx++]; auto ln1_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn1_w = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn1_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn2_w = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn2_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ln2_g = params[param_idx++]; auto ln2_b = params[param_idx++]; // Self-attention auto q = torch::matmul(hidden, q_w.t()) + q_b; auto k = torch::matmul(hidden, k_w.t()) + k_b; auto v = torch::matmul(hidden, v_w.t()) + v_b; // Reshape for multi-head q = q.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); k = k.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); v = v.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); // Scaled dot-product attention auto scores = torch::matmul(q, k.transpose(-2, -1)) * scale; // Causal mask auto causal_mask = torch::triu(torch::full({seq_len, seq_len}, -INFINITY, scores.options()), 1); scores = scores + causal_mask.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(0); auto probs = torch::softmax(scores, -1); auto attn_out = torch::matmul(probs, v); // Reshape back attn_out = attn_out.permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).reshape({batch_size, seq_len, hidden_size}); attn_out = torch::matmul(attn_out, o_w.t()) + o_b; // Residual + layer norm hidden = hidden + attn_out; hidden = custom_layer_norm(hidden, ln1_g, ln1_b, eps); // FFN auto ffn1 = torch::matmul(hidden, ffn1_w.t()) + ffn1_b; ffn1 = torch::gelu(ffn1); auto ffn2 = torch::matmul(ffn1, ffn2_w.t()) + ffn2_b; // Residual + layer norm hidden = hidden + ffn2; hidden = custom_layer_norm(hidden, ln2_g, ln2_b, eps); } auto lm_head_w = params[param_idx++]; auto lm_head_b = params[param_idx++]; auto logits = torch::matmul(hidden, lm_head_w.t()) + lm_head_b; return logits; } ``` Wait, there are several issues: 1. `torch::nn::functional::embedding` - I think the right ATen function is `torch::embedding` or `at::embedding` 2. `q_w.t()` for transposing - in ATen this is `.t()` for 2D tensors 3. Here's my first draft: ```python import torch from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline cuda_source = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cmath> __global__ void layer_norm_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ output, int num_rows, int hidden_size, float eps) { int row = blockIdx.x; if (row >= num_rows) return; int tid = threadIdx.x; const float* row_in = input + row * hidden_size; float* row_out = output + row * hidden_size; extern __shared__ float sdata[]; float sum = 0.0f; #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { sum += row_in[i]; } sdata[tid] = sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); float mean = sdata[0]; float var_sum = 0.0f; #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float diff = row_in[i] - mean; var_sum += diff * diff; } sdata[tid] = var_sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); float variance = sdata[0]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(variance + eps); #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float val = (row_in[i] - mean) * inv_std; row_out[i] = val * gamma[i] + beta[i]; } } torch::Tensor custom_layer_norm(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor gamma, torch::Tensor beta, float eps) { int batch_size = input.size(0); int seq_len = input.size(1); int hidden_size = input.size(2); int num_rows = batch_size * seq_len; auto output = torch::empty_like(input); int threads = 256; int shared_mem = threads * sizeof(float); layer_norm_kernel<<<num_rows, threads, shared_mem>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), gamma.data_ptr<float>(), beta.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), num_rows, hidden_size, eps ); return output; } torch::Tensor transformer_forward( torch::Tensor input_ids, std::vector<torch::Tensor> params, int num_layers, int num_heads, int vocab_size, float eps) { int param_idx = 0; auto word_emb = params[param_idx++]; auto pos_emb = params[param_idx++]; auto embed_ln_gamma = params[param_idx++]; auto embed_ln_beta = params[param_idx++]; int batch_size = input_ids.size(0); int seq_len = input_ids.size(1); int hidden_size = word_emb.size(1); int head_dim = hidden_size / num_heads; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf(head_dim); // Embedding lookup auto hidden = torch::embedding(word_emb, input_ids); // Position embeddings if (pos_emb.numel() > 0) { auto pos_ids = torch::arange(seq_len, input_ids.options().dtype(torch::kLong)); auto pos_embeds = torch::embedding(pos_emb, pos_ids).unsqueeze(0); hidden = hidden + pos_embeds; } // Embedding layer norm hidden = custom_layer_norm(hidden, embed_ln_gamma, embed_ln_beta, eps); // Causal mask auto causal_mask = torch::triu( torch::full({seq_len, seq_len}, -INFINITY, hidden.options()), 1 ).unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(0); for (int layer = 0; layer < num_layers; layer++) { auto q_w = params[param_idx++]; auto q_b = params[param_idx++]; auto k_w = params[param_idx++]; auto k_b = params[param_idx++]; auto v_w = params[param_idx++]; auto v_b = params[param_idx++]; auto o_w = params[param_idx++]; auto o_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ln1_g = params[param_idx++]; auto ln1_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn1_w = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn1_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn2_w = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn2_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ln2_g = params[param_idx++]; auto ln2_b = params[param_idx++]; // Self-attention with Post-LN auto q = at::matmul(hidden, q_w.t()) + q_b; auto k = at::matmul(hidden, k_w.t()) + k_b; auto v = at::matmul(hidden, v_w.t()) + v_b; q = q.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); k = k.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); v = v.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); auto scores = at::matmul(q, k.transpose(-2, -1)) * scale; scores = scores + causal_mask; auto probs = at::softmax(scores, -1); auto attn_out = at::matmul(probs, v); attn_out = attn_out.permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).reshape({batch_size, seq_len, hidden_size}); attn_out = at::matmul(attn_out, o_w.t()) + o_b; hidden = hidden + attn_out; hidden = custom_layer_norm(hidden, ln1_g, ln1_b, eps); auto ffn1 = at::matmul(hidden, ffn1_w.t()) + ffn1_b; ffn1 = torch::gelu(ffn1); auto ffn2 = at::matmul(ffn1, ffn2_w.t()) + ffn2_b; hidden = hidden + ffn2; hidden = custom_layer_norm(hidden, ln2_g, ln2_b, eps); } auto lm_head_w = params[param_idx++]; auto lm_head_b = params[param_idx++]; auto logits = at::matmul(hidden, lm_head_w.t()) + lm_head_b; return logits; } ''' module = load_inline( name="bigbird_custom", cpp_sources=cuda_source, functions=["transformer_forward"], extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"], build_directory="/tmp/bigbird_build" ) class ModelNew(torch.nn.Module): def __init__(self, model_name, config): super().__init__() from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM self.model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(model_name, config=config) self.model.eval() self.num_layers = self.model.config.num_hidden_layers self.num_heads = self.model.config.num_attention_heads self.hidden_size = self.model.config.hidden_size self.vocab_size = self.model.config.vocab_size self.eps = getattr(self.model.config, 'layer_norm_eps', 1e-12) self._extract_params() def 'LayerNorm', getattr(embed_module, 'layer_norm', None)) embed_ln_gamma = embed_ln.weight embed_ln_beta = embed_ln.bias params = [word_emb, pos_emb, embed_ln_gamma, embed_ln_beta] for layer in encoder.layer: # Attention attn_self = layer.attention.self q_w = attn_self.query.weight q_b = attn_self.query.bias k_w = attn_self.key.weight k_b = attn_self.key.bias v_w = attn_self.value.weight v_b = attn_self.value.bias # Attention output attn_out = layer.attention.output o_w = attn_out.dense.weight o_b = attn_out.dense.bias ln1 = getattr(attn_out, 'LayerNorm', getattr(attn_out, 'layer_norm', None)) ln1_g = ln1.weight ln1_b = ln1.bias # Intermediate intermediate = layer.intermediate ffn1_w = intermediate.dense.weight ffn1_b = intermediate.dense.bias # Output output = layer.output ffn2_w = output.dense.weight ffn2_b = output.dense.bias ln2 = getattr(output, 'LayerNorm', getattr(output, 'layer_norm', None)) ln2_g = ln2.weight ln2_b = ln2.bias params.extend([q_w, q_b, k_w, k_b, v_w, v_b, o_w, o_b, ln1_g, ln1_b, ffn1_w, ffn1_b, ffn2_w, ffn2_b, ln2_g, ln2_b]) # LM head if hasattr(self.model, 'cls'): lm_head_w = self.model.cls.predictions.decoder.weight lm_head_b = is None: lm_head_b = torch.zeros(self.vocab_size, dtype=word_emb.dtype, device=word_emb.device) params.extend([lm_head_w, lm_head_b]) # Convert to contiguous float tensors self.params = One final thought: should I pre-transpose weights in Python to avoid `.t()` in C++? This might give a slight speedup since we avoid the transpose view creation. But `.t()` is essentially just a metadata operation, not a memory copy. Actually, for non-contiguous tensors, `.t()` creates a view. If the weights are already contiguous and 2D, `.t()` is a view with swapped strides. This doesn't copy memory. So the overhead is negligible. But there's a catch: cuBLAS matrix multiplication might need specific memory layouts for optimal performance. When we do `hidden @ weight.t()`, where weight is stored as [out, in], `.t()` creates a logical view as [in, out] but with non-contiguous strides if the original was row-major. Actually, in PyTorch, 2D tensors are row-major. `weight` of shape [out, in] is stored in memory as [out][in]. The transpose view `.t()` has shape [in, out] but with strides (1, in). This is actually a COLUMN-MAJOR view of a row-major matrix. For `matmul(A, B)` where A is [B, S, in] and B is [in, out] (contiguous row-major), cuBLAS computes C = A * B. But if B has non-standard strides, cuBLAS might need to copy it. For `matmul(hidden, weight.t())` where `weight.t()` has shape [in, out] and strides (1, in), is this efficient? Actually, matmul with a transposed weight is very common. PyTorch handles it efficiently by telling cuBLAS to compute `C = A * B^T` where B is the original weight matrix. But in my code, I explicitly call `.t()` first. Does PyTorch optimize this? When `.t()` creates a view with transposed strides, subsequent `matmul` might see that the tensor is non-contiguous. For 2D tensors, `matmul` can handle transposed inputs efficiently. For my code, `q_w` is contiguous [out, in]. `q_w.t()` is a view [in, out] with transposed strides. `at::matmul(hidden, q_w.t())` should be as efficient as `F.linear(hidden, q_w)` in Python. If I want to avoid any overhead, I could pre-transpose weights in Python and store them as contiguous [in, out] tensors. This would make `matmul(hidden, q_w_transposed)` use a contiguous weight matrix. Let me do this in Python: ```python q_w = attn_self.query.weight.t().contiguous() ``` Then in C++: ```cpp auto q = at::matmul(hidden, q_w) + q_b; ``` This avoids the `.t()` call in C++ and ensures the weight is in a matmul-friendly layout. Yes, let me do this. I'll transpose all weights in Python before passing to C++. Let me write it: ```python import torch from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline cuda_source = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cmath> #include <limits> __global__ void layer_norm_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ output, int num_rows, int hidden_size, float eps) { int row = blockIdx.x; if (row >= num_rows) return; int tid = threadIdx.x; const float* row_in = input + row * hidden_size; float* row_out = output + row * hidden_size; extern __shared__ float sdata[]; float sum = 0.0f; #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { sum += row_in[i]; } sdata[tid] = sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); float mean = sdata[0]; float var_sum = 0.0f; #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float diff = row_in[i] - mean; var_sum += diff * diff; } sdata[tid] = var_sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); float variance = sdata[0]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(variance + eps); #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float val = (row_in[i] - mean) * inv_std; row_out[i] = val * gamma[i] + beta[i]; } } torch::Tensor custom_layer_norm(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor gamma, torch::Tensor beta, float eps) { int batch_size = input.size(0); int seq_len = input.size(1); int hidden_size = input.size(2); int num_rows = batch_size * seq_len; auto output = torch::empty_like(input); int threads = 256; int shared_mem = threads * sizeof(float); layer_norm_kernel<<<num_rows, threads, shared_mem>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), gamma.data_ptr<float>(), beta.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), num_rows, hidden_size, eps ); return output; } torch::Tensor transformer_layers_forward( torch::Tensor hidden, std::vector<torch::Tensor> params, int num_layers, int num_heads, float eps) { torch::NoGradGuard no_grad; int param_idx = 0; int batch_size = hidden.size(0); int seq_len = hidden.size(1); int hidden_size = hidden.size(2); int head_dim = hidden_size / num_heads; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)head_dim); // Causal mask auto causal_mask = torch::triu( torch::full({seq_len, seq_len}, -std::numeric_limits<float>::infinity(), hidden.options()), 1 ).unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(0); for (int layer = 0; layer < num_layers; layer++) { auto q_w = params[param_idx++]; auto q_b = params[param_idx++]; auto k_w = params[param_idx++]; auto k_b = params[param_idx++]; auto v_w = params[param_idx++]; auto v_b = params[param_idx++]; auto o_w = params[param_idx++]; auto o_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ln1_g = params[param_idx++]; auto ln1_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn1_w = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn1_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn2_w = params[param_idx++]; auto ffn2_b = params[param_idx++]; auto ln2_g = params[param_idx++]; auto ln2_b = params[param_idx++]; // Self-attention auto q = at::matmul(hidden, q_w) + q_b; auto k = at::matmul(hidden, k_w) + k_b; auto v = at::matmul(hidden, v_w) + v_b; q = q.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); k = k.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); v = v.view({batch_size, seq_len, num_heads, head_dim}).permute({0, 2, 1, 3}); auto scores = at::matmul(q, k.transpose(-2, -1)) * scale; scores = scores + causal_mask; auto probs = at::softmax(scores, -1); auto attn_out = at::matmul(probs, v); attn_out = attn_out.permute({0, 2, 1, 3}).reshape({batch_size, seq_len, hidden_size}); attn_out = at::matmul(attn_out, o_w) + o_b; hidden = hidden + attn_out; hidden = custom_layer_norm(hidden, ln1_g, ln1_b, eps); // FFN auto ffn1 = at::matmul(hidden, ffn1_w) + ffn1_b; ffn1 = torch::gelu(ffn1); auto ffn2 = at::matmul(ffn1, ffn2_w) + ffn2_b; hidden = hidden + ffn2; hidden = custom_layer_norm(hidden, ln2_g, ln2_b, eps); } auto lm_dense_w = params[param_idx++]; auto lm_dense_b = params[param_idx++]; auto lm_ln_g = params[param_idx++]; auto lm_ln_b = params[param_idx++]; auto lm_decoder_w = params[param_idx++]; auto lm_decoder_b = params[param_idx++]; auto lm_hidden = at::matmul(hidden, lm_dense_w) + lm_dense_b; lm_hidden = torch::gelu(lm_hidden); lm_hidden = custom_layer_norm(lm_hidden, lm_ln_g, lm_ln_b, eps); auto logits = at::matmul(lm_hidden, lm_decoder_w) + lm_decoder_b; return logits; } ''' custom_module = load_inline( name="bigbird_custom", cpp_sources="", cuda_sources=cuda_source, functions=["transformer_layers_forward"], extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"], ) class ModelNew(torch.nn.Module): def __init__(self, model_name, config): super().__init__() from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM self.model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(model_name, config=config) self.model.eval() self.num_layers = self.model.config.num_hidden_layers self.num_heads = self.model.config.num_attention_heads self.eps = getattr(self.model.config, 'layer_norm_eps', 1e-12) # Extract module references and parameters self._prepare_model() def _prepare_model(self): # Find embedding module if hasattr(self.model, 'bert'): self.embed_module = self.model.bert.embeddings encoder = self.model.bert.encoder elif hasattr(self.model, 'roberta'): self.embed_module = self.model.roberta.embeddings encoder = self.model.roberta.encoder else: # Fallback - try to find embeddings by walking the model for name, module in self.model.named_modules(): if 'embeddings' in name and not hasattr(self, 'embed_module'): self.embed_module = module if 'encoder' in name and hasattr(module, 'layer'): encoder = module params = [] for layer in encoder.layer: # Attention weights - transpose for efficient matmul attn_self = layer.attention.self q_w = attn_self.query.weight.t().contiguous() q_b = attn_self.query.bias k_w = attn_self.key.weight.t().contiguous() k_b = attn_self.key.bias v_w = attn_self.value.weight.t().contiguous() v_b = attn_self.value.bias attn_out = layer.attention.output o_w = attn_out.dense.weight.t().contiguous() o_b = attn_out.dense.bias ln1 = getattr(attn_out, 'LayerNorm', getattr(attn_out, 'layer_norm', None)) ln1_g = ln1.weight ln1_b = ln1.bias intermediate = layer.intermediate ffn1_w = intermediate.dense.weight.t().contiguous() ffn1_b = intermediate.dense.bias output = layer.output ffn2_w = output.dense.weight.t().contiguous() ffn2_b = output.dense.bias ln2 = getattr(output, 'LayerNorm', getattr(output, 'layer_norm', None)) ln2_g = ln2.weight ln2_b = ln2.bias params.extend([q_w, q_b, k_w, k_b, v_w, v_b, o_w, o_b, ln1_g, ln1_b, ffn1_w, ffn1_b, ffn2_w, ffn2_b, ln2_g, ln2_b]) # LM head if hasattr(self.model, 'cls') and hasattr(self.model.cls, 'predictions'): pred = self.model.cls.predictions lm_dense_w = pred.transform.dense.weight.t().contiguous() lm_dense_b = pred.transform.dense.bias lm_ln = getattr(pred.transform, 'LayerNorm', getattr(pred.transform, 'layer_norm', None)) lm_ln_g = lm_ln.weight Now `sdata[0..63]` each holds sum of 4 original values. - s=32: NOT executed because 32 > 32 is false. So `sdata[0..31]` each holds sum of 4 original values. The warp shuffle then reduces these 32 values (each sum of 4) to get the total of 128 values. But wait, we had 256 threads originally! Where are the other 128 values? Actually, looking again: - s=128: tid < 128, so `sdata[tid] += sdata[tid+128]`. This combines 256 elements into 128. - s=64: tid < 64, so `sdata[tid] += sdata[tid+64]`. This combines 128 into 64. - s=32: NOT executed. So after s=64, `sdata[0..63]` contains 64 partial sums, each representing 4 original thread values. The warp shuffle on `tid < 32` only reads `sdata[0..31]`, which are 32 partial sums representing 4*32 = 128 original values. But we had 256 original values! What happened to elements 64-127? Ah, I see the issue. `sdata[64..127]` still contains valid partial sums (each representing 2 original values from the s=128 step). But `tid < 32` only reads `sdata[0..31]`. So we're only reducing HALF the values (128 out of 256)! This is a BUG in my reduction! The loop should continue to `s > 0` or handle the remaining elements. Let me fix it. For 256 threads, the tree should reduce all the way: - s=128: 256 -> 128 - s=64: 128 -> 64 - s=32: 64 -> 32 - Then warp shuffle: 32 -> 1 But my loop condition is `s > 32`, which means s=32 is NOT executed! So I need: ```cpp for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 0; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } ``` But then for s=16, 8, 4, 2, 1: this executes within a single warp, and `__syncthreads()` is technically not needed for threads within a warp. But it's also not harmful (it acts as a memory barrier). However, for divergent warps, `__syncthreads()` can be problematic. A cleaner approach: ```cpp for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; v += sdata[tid + 32]; // If blockDim.x > 32, combine the second warp for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v; } ``` Wait, `sdata[tid + 32]` is only valid if `tid + 32 < blockDim.x`. For `blockDim.x = 256`, `tid < 32`, so `tid + 32` ranges from 32 to 63. This is valid! And `sdata[32..63]` contains the partial sums from the `s=64` step! So adding them in the warp gives us the total. Let me trace for blockDim.x=256: 1. Initial: sdata[0..255] each has 1 value 2. s=128: tid < 128, sdata[tid] += sdata[tid+128]. Now sdata[0..127] has sums of 2 values. 3. s=64: tid < 64, sdata[tid] += sdata[tid+64]. Now sdata[0..63] has sums of 4 values. 4. Loop ends (64 > 32 is true, next is 32 > 32 is false). 5. tid < 32: read sdata[tid] (which has sum of 4 values). Then `v += sdata[tid + 32]`. sdata[tid+32] has sum of 2 values from step 2. Wait, no! After step 3 (s=64): - `sdata[0]` = original[0] + original[128] + original[64] + original[192] - `sdata[1]` = original[1] + original[129] + original[65] + original[193] - ... - `sdata[32]` = original[32] + original[160] + original[96] + original[224] So `sdata[tid]` for tid=0 is sum of 4 values. `sdata[tid+32]` for tid=0 is `sdata[32]`, which is ALSO sum of 4 values. Together they give sum of 8 values. But there are 256 values total! 8 * 32 = 256. Yes! Because we have 32 threads in the warp, each combining 2 partial sums of 4, giving 32 partial sums of 8, and then warp shuffle reduces 32 to 1. Wait, let me double check: - After s=128: each of 128 entries has 2 values -> total accounted: 256 - After s=64: each of 64 entries has 4 values -> total accounted: 256 - After `v += sdata[tid+32]`: each of 32 threads has 4+4=8 values -> total accounted: 8*32 = 256 Yes! This is correct. The warp shuffle then reduces the 32 values of 8 to 1 total. So my original code with: ```cpp if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } } ``` Is WRONG because it doesn't add `sdata[tid + 32]`. I need: ```cpp if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; if (tid + 32 < blockDim.x) { v += sdata[tid + 32]; } for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v; } ``` Wait, `tid + 32 < blockDim.x` is always true for `blockDim.x >= 64` and `tid < 32`. For `blockDim.x = 256`, yes. For `blockDim.x = 128`, `tid + 32` ranges from 32 to 63, which is < 128. For `blockDim.x = 64`, `tid + 32` ranges from 32 to 63, which is < 64. For `blockDim.x = 32`, `tid + 32` ranges from 32 to 63, which is NOT < 32. So for `blockDim.x = 32`, the condition fails. But if `blockDim.x = 32`, the shared memory loop: ```cpp for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) ``` doesn't execute at all (16 > 32 is false). So `sdata[tid]` for tid < 32 contains the original thread sums. The warp shuffle reduces 32 to 1. This is correct! So the fix is: ```cpp if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; if (blockDim.x > 32) { v += sdata[tid + 32]; } for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v; } ``` Or simpler, since we always launch with 256 threads: ```cpp if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid] + sdata[tid + 32]; for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v; } ``` I'll use the simpler version since `blockDim.x` is fixed at 256. But to be robust, I should handle the general case. Let me write it carefully. Actually, for `blockDim.x = 256`: - s=128: used - s=64: used - s=32: NOT used If `blockDim.x = 128`: - s=64: used - s=32: NOT used If `blockDim.x = 64`: - s=32: NOT used For `blockDim.x <= 32`, no shared memory reduction is used. In all cases, when we reach the warp shuffle: - `sdata[0..min(31, blockDim.x-1)]` contains partial sums - For blockDim.x > 32, `sdata[32..min(63, blockDim.x-1)]` also contains partial sums So the correct warp shuffle code: ```cpp if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; if (tid + 32 < blockDim.x) { v += sdata[tid + 32]; } for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v; } ``` Wait, if `blockDim.x = 256`, `sdata[tid]` for `tid < 32` contains a 4-element sum. `sdata[tid + 32]` also contains a 4-element sum. Together they have 8 elements. Then 32 threads each with 8 elements are reduced to 1. 8 * 32 = 256. Correct! If `blockDim.x = 128`, `sdata[tid]` for `tid < 32` contains a 2-element sum. `sdata[tid + 32]` contains a 2-element sum. Together 4 elements. 4 * 32 = 128. Correct! If `blockDim.x = 64`, `sdata[tid]` for `tid < 32` contains a 1-element sum. `sdata[tid + 32]` contains a 1-element sum. Together 2 elements. 2 * 32 = 64. Correct! If `blockDim.x = 32`, `sdata[tid]` contains a 1-element sum. `tid + 32 < 32` is false, so no addition. Warp shuffle reduces 1 * 32 = 32. Correct! This works for all power-of-2 block sizes >= 32. Good. But wait, what if `blockDim.x` is not a power of 2? Then the shared memory reduction `s = blockDim.x / 2` might not work correctly because `sdata[tid + s]` for `tid < s` would cover only half the threads, leaving the rest unaccounted for. Since I always launch with 256 threads, `blockDim.x` is always 256 (a power of 2). So it's fine. OK let me fix the layer norm kernel with this correction. Also, let me reconsider whether warpSize is 32 for H100. Yes, H100 has warp size 32. Let me write the complete corrected code: ```cuda __global__ void layer_norm_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ gamma, const float* __restrict__ beta, float* __restrict__ output, int num_rows, int hidden_size, float eps) { int row = blockIdx.x; if (row >= num_rows) return; int tid = threadIdx.x; const float* row_in = input + row * hidden_size; float* row_out = output + row * hidden_size; extern __shared__ float sdata[]; float sum = 0.0f; #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { sum += row_in[i]; } sdata[tid] = sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; if (tid + 32 < blockDim.x) { v += sdata[tid + 32]; } for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); float mean = sdata[0]; float var_sum = 0.0f; #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float diff = row_in[i] - mean; var_sum += diff * diff; } sdata[tid] = var_sum; __syncthreads(); for (int s = blockDim.x / 2; s > 32; s >>= 1) { if (tid < s) sdata[tid] += sdata[tid + s]; __syncthreads(); } if (tid < 32) { float v = sdata[tid]; if (tid + 32 < blockDim.x) { v += sdata[tid + 32]; } for (int offset = warpSize / 2; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { v += __shfl_down_sync(0xFFFFFFFF, v, offset); } if (tid == 0) sdata[0] = v / hidden_size; } __syncthreads(); float variance = sdata[0]; float inv_std = rsqrtf(variance + eps); #pragma unroll 4 for (int i = tid; i < hidden_size; i += blockDim.x) { float val = (row_in[i] - mean) * inv_std; row_out[i] = val * gamma[i] + beta[i]; } } ``` This looks correct now. Looking at the transformers source for BERT: ```python class BertLayer(nn.Module): def __init__(self, config): super().__init__() self.attention = BertAttention(config) self.intermediate = BertIntermediate(config) self.output = BertOutput(config) def forward(self, hidden_states, ...): self_attention_outputs = self.attention(hidden_states, ...) attention_output = self_attention_outputs[0] intermediate_output = self.intermediate(attention_output) layer_output = self.output(intermediate_output, attention_output) return (layer_output,) ``` And `BertAttention`: ```python class BertAttention(nn.Module): def forward(self, hidden_states, ...): self_outputs = self.self(hidden_states, ...) attention_output = self.output(self_outputs[0], hidden_states) return (attention_output, ...) ``` And `BertSelfOutput`: ```python class BertSelfOutput(nn.Module): def __init__(self, config): super().__init__() self.dense = nn.Linear(config.hidden_size, config.hidden_size) self.LayerNorm = nn.LayerNorm(config.hidden_size, eps=config.layer_norm_eps) self.dropout = nn.Dropout(config.hidden_dropout_prob) def forward(self, hidden_states, input_tensor): hidden_states = self.dense(hidden_states) hidden_states = self.dropout(hidden_states) hidden_states = self.LayerNorm(hidden_states + input_tensor) return hidden_states ``` And `BertOutput`: ```python class BertOutput(nn.Module): def __init__(self, config): super().__init__() self.dense = nn.Linear(config.intermediate_size, config.hidden_size) self.LayerNorm = nn.LayerNorm(config.hidden_size, eps=config.layer_norm_eps) self.dropout = nn.Dropout(config.hidden_dropout_prob) def forward(self, hidden_states, input_tensor): hidden_states = self.dense(hidden_states) hidden_states = self.dropout(hidden_states) hidden_states = self.LayerNorm(hidden_states + input_tensor) return hidden_states ``` So the actual structure is: 1. Self-attention produces `attn_raw` 2. `BertSelfOutput` does: dense(attn_raw) -> dropout -> LayerNorm(dense_output + hidden_input) 3. `BertIntermediate` does: dense(hidden) -> GELU 4. `BertOutput` does: dense(intermediate) -> dropout -> LayerNorm(dense_output + attention_output) So the sequence is: ``` attn_raw = self_attention(hidden) attn_out = dense(attn_raw) attn_out = dropout(attn_out) hidden = LayerNorm(attn_out + hidden) # This is the attention output LayerNorm ffn1 = dense(hidden) ffn1 = GELU(ffn1) ffn2 = dense(ffn1) ffn2 = dropout(ffn2) hidden = LayerNorm(ffn2 + hidden) # Wait, the residual is the attention output, not the FFN input! ``` Wait, `BertOutput.forward(intermediate_output, attention_output)` does `LayerNorm(dense(intermediate_output) + attention_output)`. So the residual for the FFN is the ATTENTION OUTPUT, not the hidden state AFTER attention. But in my code, I wrote: ```cpp hidden = hidden + ffn2; hidden = custom_layer_norm(hidden, ln2_g, ln2_b, eps); ``` Where `hidden` before the FFN is the output of `custom_layer_norm(hidden, ln1_g, ln1_b, eps)`, which is the attention output. This matches `BertOutput` exactly! So my code is structurally correct. Wait, let me re-verify.
